Just this simple difference in voting method ensures that both houses in India have separate interests and will act as checks against each other within theur own powers. India's President is also the highest executive officer that appoints the Prime Minister, is the commander...
...difference is further reinforced by the difference in election methods, the Lok Sabha being elected via FPTP, like most of the US House currently is, whereas the Rajya Sabha is elected via the more representative Single Transferable Vote (a multi winner variant of RCV).
...dual executive. It retains certain Westminster aspects such as the Lok Sabha being stronger and more influential than the Rajya Sabha, but the Rajya Sabha retains strong checks, notably in retaining the sovereignty of India's States against the national government. This...
The US isn't the only large republic with various checks and balances. India has a masterfully designed constitution that adopts and adapts Britain's Westminster system into a quasi-federal system with an almost...
...Electoral College, and the Supreme Court to act as a balance and final arbiter against the other three groups. Not to mention the State and Federal governments possessing balances against each. A federal system of separated powers is generally what's ideal for this country.
